Any\n    improvements to the form API should be made to this class, not to the Form\n    class.\n    \"\"\"\n\n    default_renderer = None\n    field_order = None\n    prefix = None\n    use_required_attribute = True\n\n    template_name_div = \"django/forms/div.html\"\n    template_name_p = \"django/forms/p.html\"\n    template_name_table = \"django/forms/table.html\"\n    template_name_ul = \"django/forms/ul.html\"\n    template_name_label = \"django/forms/label.html\"\n\n    bound_field_class = None\n\n    def __init__(\n        self,\n        data=None,\n        files=None,\n        auto_id=\"id_%s\",\n        prefix=None,\n        initial=None,\n        error_class=ErrorList,\n        label_suffix=None,\n        empty_permitted=False,\n        field_order=None,\n        use_required_attribute=None,\n        renderer=None,\n        bound_field_class=None,\n    ):\n        self.is_bound = data is not None or files is not None\n        self.data = MultiValueDict() if data is None else data\n        self.files = MultiValueDict() if files is None else files\n        self.auto_id = auto_id\n        if prefix is not None:\n            self.prefix = prefix\n        self.initial = initial or {}\n        self.error_class = error_class\n        # Translators: This is the default suffix added to form field labels\n        self.label_suffix = label_suffix if label_suffix is not None else _(\":\")\n        self.empty_permitted = empty_permitted\n        self._errors = None  # Stores the errors after clean() has been called.\n\n        # The base_fields class attribute is the *class-wide* definition of\n        # fields. Append\n        fields not included in the list in the default order for backward\n        compatibility with subclasses not overriding field_order. If\n        field_order is None, keep all fields in the order defined in the class.\n        Ignore unknown fields in field_order to allow disabling fields in form\n        subclasses without redefining ordering.\n        \"\"\"\n        if field_order is None:\n            return\n        fields = {}\n        for key in field_order:\n            try:\n                fields[key] = self.fields.pop(key)\n            except KeyError:  # ignore unknown fields\n                pass\n        fields.update(self.fields)  # add remaining fields in original order\n        self.fields = fields\n\n    def __repr__(self):\n        if self._errors is None:\n            is_valid = \"Unknown\"\n        else:\n            is_valid = self.is_bound and not self._errors\n        return \"<%(cls)s bound=%(bound)s, valid=%(valid)s, fields=(%(fields)s)>\" % {\n            \"cls\": self.__class__.__name__,\n            \"bound\": self.is_bound,\n            \"valid\": is_valid,\n            \"fields\": \";\".join(self.fields),\n        }\n\n    def _bound_items(self):\n        \"\"\"Yield (name, bf) pairs, where bf is a BoundField object.\"\"\"\n        for name in self.fields:\n            yield name, self[name]\n\n    def __iter__(self):\n        \"\"\"Yield the form's fields as BoundField objects.\"\"\"\n        for name in self.fields:\n            yield self[name]\n\n    def __getitem__(self, name):\n        \"\"\"Return a BoundField with the given name.\"\"\"\n        try:\n            field = self.fields[name]\n        except KeyError:\n            raise KeyError(\n                \"Key '%s' not found in '%s'. Use a global default if not specified\n        # either as an argument or as self.default_renderer.\n        if renderer is None:\n            if self.default_renderer is None:\n                renderer = get_default_renderer()\n            else:\n                renderer = self.default_renderer\n                if isinstance(self.default_renderer, type):\n                    renderer = renderer()\n        self.renderer = renderer\n\n        self.bound_field_class = (\n            bound_field_class\n            or self.bound_field_class\n            or getattr(self.renderer, \"bound_field_class\", None)\n        )\n\n    def order_fields(self, field_order):\n        \"\"\"\n        Rearrange the fields according to field_order.\n\n        field_order is a list of field names specifying the order. Append\n        fields not included in the list in the default order for backward\n        compatibility with subclasses not overriding field_order. If\n        field_order is None, keep all fields in the order defined in the class.\n        Ignore unknown fields in field_order to allow disabling fields in form\n        subclasses without redefining ordering.\n        \"\"\"\n        if field_order is None:\n            return\n        fields = {}\n        for key in field_order:\n            try:\n                fields[key] = self.fields.pop(key)\n            except KeyError:  # ignore unknown fields\n                pass\n        fields.update(self.fields)  # add remaining fields in original order\n        self.fields = fields\n\n    def __repr__(self):\n        if self._errors is None:\n            is_valid = \"Unknown\"\n        else:\n            is_valid = self.is_bound and not self._errors\n        return \"<%(cls)s bound=%(bound)s, valid=%(valid)s, fields=(%(fields)s)>\" % {\n            \"cls\": self.__class__.__name__,\n            \"bound\": self.is_bound,\n            \"valid\": is_valid,\n            \"fields\": \";\".join(self.fields),\n        }\n\n    def _bound_items(self):\n        \"\"\"Yield (name, bf) pairs, where bf is a BoundField object.\"\"\"\n        for name in self.fields:\n            yield name, self[name]\n\n    def __iter__(self):\n        \"\"\"Yield the form's fields as BoundField objects.\"\"\"\n        for name in self.fields:\n            yield self[name]\n\n    def __getitem__(self, name):\n        \"\"\"Return a BoundField with the given name.\"\"\"\n        try:\n            field = self.fields[name]\n        except KeyError:\n            raise KeyError(\n                \"Key '%s' not found in '%s'. Choices are: %s.\"\n                % (\n                    name,\n                    self.__class__.__name__,\n                    \", \".join(sorted(self.fields)),\n                )\n            )\n        if name not in self._bound_fields_cache:\n            self._bound_fields_cache[name] = field.get_bound_field(self, name)\n        return self._bound_fields_cache[name]\n\n    @property\n    def errors(self):\n        \"\"\"Return an ErrorDict for the data provided for the form.\"\"\"\n        if self._errors is None:\n            self.full_clean()\n        return self._errors\n\n    def is_valid(self):\n        \"\"\"Return True if the form has no errors, or False otherwise.\"\"\"\n        return self.is_bound and not self.errors\n\n    def add_prefix(self, field_name):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return the field name with a prefix appended, if this Form has a\n        prefix set.\n\n        Subclasses may wish to override.\n        \"\"\"\n        return \"%s-%s\" % (self.prefix, field_name) if self.prefix else field_name\n\n    def add_initial_prefix(self, field_name):\n        \"\"\"Add an 'initial' prefix for checking dynamic initial values.\"\"\"\n        return \"initial-%s\" % self.add_prefix(field_name)\n\n    def _widget_data_value(self, widget, html_name):\n        # Return an empty ErrorList if there\n        are none.\n        \"\"\"\n        return self.errors.get(\n            NON_FIELD_ERRORS,\n            self.error_class(error_class=\"nonfield\", renderer=self.renderer),\n        )\n\n    def add_error(self, field, error):\n        \"\"\"\n        Update the content of `self._errors`.\n\n        The `field` argument is the name of the field to which the errors\n        should be added. If it's None, treat the errors as NON_FIELD_ERRORS.\n\n        The `error` argument can be a single error, a list of errors, or a\n        dictionary that maps field names to lists of errors. An \"error\" can be\n        either a simple string or an instance of ValidationError with its\n        message attribute set and a \"list or dictionary\" can be an actual\n        `list` or `dict` or an instance of ValidationError with its\n        `error_list` or `error_dict` attribute set.\n\n        If `error` is a dictionary, the `field` argument *must* be None and\n        errors will be added to the fields that correspond to the keys of the\n        dictionary.\n        \"\"\"\n        if not isinstance(error, ValidationError):\n            # Used for model validation in model forms.\n        \"\"\"\n        pass\n\n    def clean(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Hook for doing any extra form-wide cleaning after Field.clean() has\n        been called on every field. Any ValidationError raised by this method\n        will not be associated with a particular field; it will have a\n        special-case association with the field named '__all__'.\n        \"\"\"\n        return self.cleaned_data\n\n    def has_changed(self):\n        \"\"\"Return True if data differs from initial.\"\"\"\n        return bool(self.changed_data)\n\n    @cached_property\n    def changed_data(self):\n        return [name for name, bf in self._bound_items() if bf._has_changed()]\n\n    @property\n    def media(self):\n        \"\"\"Return all media required to render the widgets on this form.\"\"\"\n        media = Media()\n        for field in self.fields.values():\n            media += field.widget.media\n        return media\n\n    def is_multipart(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return True if the form needs to be multipart-encoded, i.e. it has\n        FileInput, or False otherwise.\n        \"\"\"\n        return any(field.widget.needs_multipart_form for field in self.fields.values())\n\n    def hidden_fields(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return a list of all the BoundField objects that are hidden fields.\n        Useful for manual form layout in templates.\n        \"\"\"\n        return [field for field in self if field.is_hidden]\n\n    def visible_fields(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return a list of BoundField objects that aren't hidden fields.\n        The opposite of the hidden_fields() method.\n        \"\"\"\n        return [field for field in self if not field.is_hidden]\n\n    def get_initial_for_field(self, field, field_name):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return initial data for field on form. Evaluate callable values.\n        \"\"\"\n        value = self.initial.get(field_name, field.initial)\n        if callable(value):\n            value = value()\n        # If this is an auto-generated default date, nix the microseconds\n        # for standardized handling. For example, ensuring that an\n    end_date is after a start_date.\n\n    Usage:\n        class DateRangeForm(forms.Form):\n            start_date = forms.DateField()\n            end_date = forms.DateField()\n\n            date_range_check = CompositFieldValidator(\n                validation_func=lambda start, end: start <= end,\n                field_names=['start_date', 'end_date'],\n                message=\"End date must be after start date.\"\n            )\n    \"\"\"\n\n    def __init__(self, validation_func, field_names, message):\n        \"\"\"\n        Initialize the CompositFieldValidator.\n\n        Args:\n            validation_func: A callable that takes values for the named fields\n                           (in the order specified in field_names) and returns\n                           True if validation passes, False otherwise.\n            field_names: A list of field names to validate together.\n            message: The error message to display if validation fails.\n        \"\"\"\n        self.validation_func = validation_func\n        self.field_names = field_names\n        self.message = message\n\n    def __call__(self, form):\n        \"\"\"\n        Called during form validation to check the cross-field constraint.\n\n        Args:\n            form: The form instance being validated.\n\n        Raises:\n            ValidationError: If validation fails or referenced fields don't exist.\n        \"\"\"\n        # Choices are: %s.\"\n                % (\n                    name,\n                    self.__class__.__name__,\n                    \", \".join(sorted(self.fields)),\n                )\n            )\n        if name not in self._bound_fields_cache:\n            self._bound_fields_cache[name] = field.get_bound_field(self, name)\n        return self._bound_fields_cache[name]\n\n    @property\n    def errors(self):\n        \"\"\"Return an ErrorDict for the data provided for the form.\"\"\"\n        if self._errors is None:\n            self.full_clean()\n        return self._errors\n\n    def is_valid(self):\n        \"\"\"Return True if the form has no errors, or False otherwise.\"\"\"\n        return self.is_bound and not self.errors\n\n    def add_prefix(self, field_name):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return the field name with a prefix appended, if this Form has a\n        prefix set.\n\n        Subclasses may wish to override.\n        \"\"\"\n        return \"%s-%s\" % (self.prefix, field_name) if self.prefix else field_name\n\n    def add_initial_prefix(self, field_name):\n        \"\"\"Add an 'initial' prefix for checking dynamic initial values.\"\"\"\n        return \"initial-%s\" % self.add_prefix(field_name)\n\n    def _widget_data_value(self, widget, html_name):\n        # Return an empty ErrorList if there\n        are none.\n        \"\"\"\n        return self.errors.get(\n            NON_FIELD_ERRORS,\n            self.error_class(error_class=\"nonfield\", renderer=self.renderer),\n        )\n\n    def add_error(self, field, error):\n        \"\"\"\n        Update the content of `self._errors`.\n\n        The `field` argument is the name of the field to which the errors\n        should be added. If it's None, treat the errors as NON_FIELD_ERRORS.\n\n        The `error` argument can be a single error, a list of errors, or a\n        dictionary that maps field names to lists of errors. An \"error\" can be\n        either a simple string or an instance of ValidationError with its\n        message attribute set and a \"list or dictionary\" can be an actual\n        `list` or `dict` or an instance of ValidationError with its\n        `error_list` or `error_dict` attribute set.\n\n        If `error` is a dictionary, the `field` argument *must* be None and\n        errors will be added to the fields that correspond to the keys of the\n        dictionary.\n        \"\"\"\n        if not isinstance(error, ValidationError):\n            # Normalize to ValidationError and let its constructor\n            # do the hard work of making sense of the input.\n            error = ValidationError(error)\n\n        if hasattr(error, \"error_dict\"):\n            if field is not None:\n                raise TypeError(\n                    \"The argument `field` must be `None` when the `error` \"\n                    \"argument is a dictionary.\"\n                )\n            else:\n                error = error.error_dict\n        else:\n            error = {field or NON_FIELD_ERRORS: error.error_list}\n\n        for field, error_list in error.items():\n            if field not in self.errors:\n                if field != NON_FIELD_ERRORS and field not in self.fields:\n                    raise ValueError(\n                        \"'%s' has no field named '%s'.\"\n                        % (self.__class__.__name__, field)\n                    )\n                if field == NON_FIELD_ERRORS:\n                    self._errors[field] = self.error_class(\n                        error_class=\"nonfield\", renderer=self.renderer\n                    )\n                else:\n                    self._errors[field] = self.error_class(\n                        renderer=self.renderer,\n                        field_id=self[field].auto_id,\n                    )\n            self._errors[field].extend(error_list)\n            if field in self.cleaned_data:\n                del self.cleaned_data[field]\n\n    def has_error(self, field, code=None):\n        return field in self.errors and (\n            code is None\n            or any(error.code == code for error in self.errors.as_data()[field])\n        )\n\n    def full_clean(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Clean all of self.data and populate self._errors and self.cleaned_data.\n        \"\"\"\n        self._errors = ErrorDict(renderer=self.renderer)\n        if not self.is_bound:  # Stop further processing.\n            return\n        self.cleaned_data = {}\n        # If the form is permitted to be empty, and none of the form data has\n        # changed from the initial data, short circuit any validation.\n        if self.empty_permitted and not self.has_changed():\n            return\n\n        self._clean_fields()\n        self._clean_form()\n        self._post_clean()\n\n    def _clean_fields(self):\n        for name, bf in self._bound_items():\n            field = bf.field\n            try:\n                self.cleaned_data[name] = field._clean_bound_field(bf)\n                if hasattr(self, \"clean_%s\" % name):\n                    value = getattr(self, \"clean_%s\" % name)()\n                    self.cleaned_data[name] = value\n            except ValidationError as e:\n                self.add_error(name, e)\n\n    def _clean_form(self):\n        try:\n            cleaned_data = self.clean()\n        except ValidationError as e:\n            self.add_error(None, e)\n        else:\n            if cleaned_data is not None:\n                self.cleaned_data = cleaned_data\n\n        # Run CompositFieldValidator instances\n        self._run_composite_validators()\n\n    def _run_composite_validators(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Run all CompositFieldValidator instances declared on this form.\n        \"\"\"\n        for validator in self.declared_validators.values():\n            try:\n                validator(self)\n            except ValidationError as e:\n                # Add the error as a non-field error (associated with '__all__')\n                self.add_error(None, e)\n\n    def _post_clean(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        An internal hook for performing additional cleaning after form cleaning\n        is complete. Used for model validation in model forms.\n        \"\"\"\n        pass\n\n    def clean(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Hook for doing any extra form-wide cleaning after Field.clean() has\n        been called on every field. Any ValidationError raised by this method\n        will not be associated with a particular field; it will have a\n        special-case association with the field named '__all__'.\n        \"\"\"\n        return self.cleaned_data\n\n    def has_changed(self):\n        \"\"\"Return True if data differs from initial.\"\"\"\n        return bool(self.changed_data)\n\n    @cached_property\n    def changed_data(self):\n        return [name for name, bf in self._bound_items() if bf._has_changed()]\n\n    @property\n    def media(self):\n        \"\"\"Return all media required to render the widgets on this form.\"\"\"\n        media = Media()\n        for field in self.fields.values():\n            media += field.widget.media\n        return media\n\n    def is_multipart(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return True if the form needs to be multipart-encoded, i.e. it has\n        FileInput, or False otherwise.\n        \"\"\"\n        return any(field.widget.needs_multipart_form for field in self.fields.values())\n\n    def hidden_fields(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return a list of all the BoundField objects that are hidden fields.\n        Useful for manual form layout in templates.\n        \"\"\"\n        return [field for field in self if field.is_hidden]\n\n    def visible_fields(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return a list of BoundField objects that aren't hidden fields.\n        The opposite of the hidden_fields() method.\n        \"\"\"\n        return [field for field in self if not field.is_hidden]\n\n    def get_initial_for_field(self, field, field_name):\n        \"\"\"\n        Return initial data for field on form. Use initial data from the form\n        or the field, in that order. Evaluate callable values.\n        \"\"\"\n        value = self.initial.get(field_name, field.initial)\n        if callable(value):\n            value = value()\n        # If this is an auto-generated default date, nix the microseconds\n        # for standardized handling. See #22502.\n        if (\n            isinstance(value, (datetime.datetime, datetime.time))\n            and not field.widget.supports_microseconds\n        ):\n            value = value.replace(microsecond=0)\n        return value\n\n\nclass Form(BaseForm, metaclass=DeclarativeFieldsMetaclass):\n    \"A collection of Fields, plus their associated data.\"\n\n    # This is a separate class from BaseForm in order to abstract the way\n    # self.fields is specified. This class (Form) is the one that does the\n    # fancy metaclass stuff purely for the semantic sugar -- it allows one\n    # to define a form using declarative syntax.\n    # BaseForm itself has no way of designating self.fields.\n","structuredPatch":[{"oldStart":389,"oldLines":6,"newStart":389,"newLines":9,"lines":["             except ValidationError as e:","                 # Add the error as a non-field error (associated with '__all__')","                 self.add_error(None, e)","+            except ValueError as e:","+                # Handle missing fields gracefully by adding as a non-field error","+                self.add_error(None, ValidationError(str(e)))"," ","     def _post_clean(self):","         \"\"\""]}],"userModified":false,"replaceAll":false}}

{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_016rzCYXn3X7fPUPs12YFmbr","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01Txa21kyKs7pxvQvFenhCJK","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/COMPOSITE_FIELD_VALIDATOR_EXAMPLE.md","content":"# CompositFieldValidator Usage Examples\n\nThe `CompositFieldValidator` is a form validator that allows you to validate relationships between multiple form fields simultaneously. This is useful for cross-field validation where you need to ensure that values across multiple fields meet certain conditions.\n\n## Basic Usage\n\n```python\nfrom django import forms\nfrom django.forms.validators import CompositFieldValidator\n\nclass DateRangeForm(forms.Form):\n    start_date = forms.DateField()\n    end_date = forms.DateField()\n\n    # Validator to ensure end_date is after start_date\n    date_range_check = CompositFieldValidator(\n        validation_func=lambda start, end: start <= end,\n        field_names=['start_date', 'end_date'],\n        message=\"End date must be after or equal to start date.\"\n    )\n```\n\n## How It Works\n\n1. **Create a validator instance** as a class attribute on your form\n2. **Specify the validation function** - a callable that receives the field values as arguments\n3. **List the field names** to validate together (in order)\n4. **Provide an error message** that will be displayed if validation fails\n\n## Validation Function\n\nThe `validation_func` parameter should be a callable that:\n- Receives values for each field in the order specified in `field_names`\n- Returns `True` if validation passes, `False` if it fails\n- Can raise an exception if needed (will be caught and treated as a validation error)\n\n## Examples\n\n### Email Confirmation\n\n```python\nclass RegistrationForm(forms.Form):\n    email = forms.EmailField()\n    email_confirm = forms.EmailField()\n\n    email_match = CompositFieldValidator(\n        validation_func=lambda email, confirm: email == confirm,\n        field_names=['email', 'email_confirm'],\n        message=\"Email addresses do not match.\"\n    )\n```\n\n### Password Validation\n\n```python\nclass PasswordForm(forms.Form):\n    password = forms.CharField(widget=forms.PasswordInput)\n    password_confirm = forms.CharField(widget=forms.PasswordInput)\n    password_length = forms.IntegerField()\n\n    password_match = CompositFieldValidator(\n        validation_func=lambda p, p_conf: p == p_conf,\n        field_names=['password', 'password_confirm'],\n        message=\"Passwords do not match.\"\n    )\n\n    password_long_enough = CompositFieldValidator(\n        validation_func=lambda p, min_len: len(p) >= min_len,\n        field_names=['password', 'password_length'],\n        message=\"Password is shorter than the minimum required length.\"\n    )\n```\n\n### Numeric Range Validation\n\n```python\nclass RangeForm(forms.Form):\n    min_value = forms.IntegerField()\n    max_value = forms.IntegerField()\n\n    valid_range = CompositFieldValidator(\n        validation_func=lambda min_v, max_v: min_v <= max_v,\n        field_names=['min_value', 'max_value'],\n        message=\"Minimum value cannot be greater than maximum value.\"\n    )\n```\n\n### Multiple Validators on Same Form\n\n```python\nclass ComplexForm(forms.Form):\n    start_date = forms.DateField()\n    end_date = forms.DateField()\n    min_duration_days = forms.IntegerField()\n\n    # Check that end_date is after start_date\n    date_order = CompositFieldValidator(\n        validation_func=lambda start, end: start <= end,\n        field_names=['start_date', 'end_date'],\n        message=\"End date must be after start date.\"\n    )\n\n    # Check that the date range meets minimum duration\n    duration_check = CompositFieldValidator(\n        validation_func=lambda start, end, min_days: (end - start).days >= min_days,\n        field_names=['start_date', 'end_date', 'min_duration_days'],\n        message=\"The date range is shorter than the minimum required duration.\"\n    )\n```\n\n## Error Handling\n\nIf validation fails, the error is added as a non-field error (associated with the form's `__all__` field). This means:\n\n```python\nform = DateRangeForm(data={'start_date': '2024-01-02', 'end_date': '2024-01-01'})\nif not form.is_valid():\n    # Access non-field errors\n    print(form.non_field_errors())  # [\"End date must be after or equal to start date.\"]\n\n    # Or access all errors\n    print(form.errors)  # {'__all__': [\"End date must be after or equal to start date.\"]}\n```\n\n## Important Notes\n\n1. **Missing Fields**: If a referenced field doesn't exist on the form, an error will be added to the form errors with a descriptive message.\n\n2. **Field Validation Errors**: If one of the referenced fields has a validation error (e.g., invalid date format), the validator will still run but the field value will be `None` in `cleaned_data`.\n\n3. **Unbound Forms**: Validators only run on bound forms (forms with data). Unbound forms skip validation.\n\n4. **Inheritance**: Validators are inherited from parent form classes, similar to fields.\n\n5. **Order**: Validators run after all field-level validation and after the form's `clean()` method, ensuring that all field data has been properly cleaned before cross-field validation.\n\n## Implementation Details\n\nThe `CompositFieldValidator` integrates with Django's form validation pipeline:\n- It's collected by the form's metaclass (similar to fields)\n- It runs during the `_clean_form()` phase of validation\n- It uses Django's standard `ValidationError` for error reporting\n- Errors are added as non-field errors to maintain consistency with form-level validation\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":0,"cache_creation_input_tokens":142,"cache_read_input_tokens":60813,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":142},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"f3548e0f-0ff4-4a11-9536-0d09eeb5d70a","uuid":"9a444429-10f7-46d6-bd6a-a42b35adda48"}

Integration Point\nValidators run during the `_clean_form()` phase, specifically after the form's `clean()` method. This ensures:\n- All field-level validation has completed\n- All field values are in `cleaned_data`\n- Custom form clean methods have executed\n- Cross-field validation is the last step before validation completes\n\n### 2. Error Handling\nValidators raise `ValidationError` which is caught and added as a non-field error (associated with `__all__`). This maintains consistency with Django's form validation patterns.\n\n### 3. Missing Field Handling\nIf a referenced field doesn't exist on the form:\n1. The validator raises a `ValueError`\n2. This is caught in `_run_composite_validators()`\n3. Converted to a `ValidationError` and added as a non-field error\n4. The form becomes invalid with a descriptive error message\n\n### 4.
